## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via rate laws. With only t and A available, the most likely models are autonomous or time-varying kinetic ODEs expressing consumption/production rates as functions of concentration and possibly explicit time dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface/photochemical regimes where rate is independent of A over a range)
- Constant production/feeding: dA_dt = c0 (source term, dosing, or generation at constant rate)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decomposition, radioactive-like decay, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Linear with offset (source + decay): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (combined constant generation and first-order loss; sign of c1 sets stability)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or 2A -> products)
- Mixed first+second order: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel unimolecular and bimolecular loss pathways)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical rate order or lumped radical-chain behavior)
- Autocatalytic / self-limiting growth-consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with depletion/finite capacity; logistic-form kinetics for concentration)
- Reversible first-order toward equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (A interconverts with a pool of size c2; net drift to equilibrium)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant (exponentially changing conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (e.g., temperature/light intensity ramps captured phenomenologically)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant (polynomial drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slowly varying environment or catalyst activity drift)
- Rational inhibition/transport-limited loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases ~A at low A and saturates at high A due to limitation/inhibition)
- Chain-branching-like sensitivity: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (highly nonlinear acceleration of loss with concentration, used as a phenomenological surrogate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Autonomous kinetics indicator: if dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), trajectories with different initial A follow the same phase-line; expect dA_dt = f(A).
- Consumption vs production: a predominantly negative dA_dt for A > 0 suggests depletion reactions; a positive region suggests net formation or autocatalysis.
- Reaction order signature: linear dependence on A implies pseudo-first-order; quadratic dependence implies bimolecular/self-reaction; non-integer power implies empirical/lumped mechanisms.
- Steady-state/equilibrium concentration: presence of (A - c) factor implies a fixed point at A = c; sign determines stability (relaxation toward or away from c).
- Parallel pathways: sums like -(c0*A + c1*A**2) indicate multiple concurrent mechanisms with different orders dominating in different A ranges.
- Reversibility: opposing linear terms (e.g., -c0*A + c1*(c2-A)) imply drift toward an equilibrium set by rate-constant ratios and total pool c2.
- Capacity or depletion effects: factors like (c1 - A) imply a finite limiting concentration and slow-down near A ≈ c1 (self-limiting/autocatalytic saturation).
- Time-dependent forcing: explicit t dependence in the effective rate (e.g., exp(c*t), c0+c1*t) indicates changing external conditions (temperature, illumination, catalyst deactivation) not captured by A alone.
- Transport/inhibition limitation: rational forms A/(1+c*A) produce an approximately first-order regime at low A and an approximately zero-order regime at high A, consistent with saturation or diffusion limits.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK20)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_p*sin(c3*A)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function of two variables
\[
f(t,A)= -0.3122128846\,A\,e^{-0.07984001874\,t} \;+\; 0.4717280564\,\sin(0.8721876285\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible as “(constant)\(\cdot A\cdot e^{(constant)\,t}\) + (constant)\(\cdot \sin((constant)\,A)\)” with **no extra dependence on \(t\)** inside the sine term, **no phase shift**, and **no extra additive terms** (unless they can be set to 0).

---

### 1. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5`
Set \(c4=0\) (no phase), \(c5=0\) (no offset). Then choose \(c0=-0.3122128846\), \(c1=-0.07984001874\), \(c2=0.4717280564\), \(c3=0.8721876285\). Matches exactly.

### 2. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`
Same as (1) but without \(+c5\). Set \(c4=0\), and choose \(c0,c1,c2,c3\) as above. Matches exactly.

### 3. `A**2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7)`
To match GT, the sine term must have **no** \(t\)-dependent prefactor, so need \(c5=0\). Also need no phase: \(c7=0\). Need no extra terms: set \(c0=0\) (kill \(A^2\)) and \(c3=0\) (kill constant). Then it becomes \(A*c1 e^{c2 t} + c4\sin(A c6)\), which can match by setting \(c1=-0.3122128846\), \(c2=-0.07984001874\), \(c4=0.4717280564\), \(c6=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 4. `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A**2*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`
Need to remove \(A*c0\): set \(c0=0\). Remove log term: set \(c3=0\). Remove \(t\) from sine prefactor: set \(c7=0\). Remove phase: \(c9=0\). Then it becomes \(A*c1 e^{c2 t} + c6\sin(A c8)\) and can match with \(c1=-0.3122128846\), \(c2=-0.07984001874\), \(c6=0.4717280564\), \(c8=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 5. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7)`
Must kill \(A^2\): \(c0=0\). Must kill linear \(A\) term: \(c1=0\). Sine prefactor must be \(t\)-independent: \(c5=0\). Phase must be 0: \(c7=0\). Then \(A*c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\sin(A c6)\) matches with \(c2=-0.3122128846\), \(c3=-0.07984001874\), \(c4=0.4717280564\), \(c6=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 6. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6 + c7*exp(c8*t)*log(c9*Abs(A) + 1)`
Even if we set \(c0=c1=c6=c7=0\), we are left with \(c2 e^{c3 t}\sin(A c4 + c5)\), which is a **product** of \(t\)-dependent exponential and sine. GT is a **sum** of an exponential-in-\(t\) term and a sine-in-\(A\) term. There is no way to make \(e^{c3 t}\sin(\cdot)\) equal to \(\sin(0.872A)\) for all \(t\) unless \(c3=0\), but then it becomes just a sine term and cannot also produce the required \(A e^{-0.07984 t}\) term. No match.

### 7. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*exp(A*c4)*exp(c5*t) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`
To get GT’s sine term, we’d need \(c7=0\) and \(c9=0\), and then \(c6\sin(A c8)\) is fine. But the exponential-in-\(t\) term in GT is \(A e^{k t}\) with no extra \(A\)-nonlinearities. The third term here includes \(A^{c2} e^{A c4} e^{c5 t}\). To reduce to \(A e^{c5 t}\), we’d need \(c4=0\) and \(c2=1\). Then it becomes \(A*c3 e^{c5 t}\), good. Also must kill \(A^2\) and \(A\) extra: set \(c0=0, c1=0\). Then we can match with \(c3=-0.3122128846\), \(c5=-0.07984001874\), \(c6=0.4717280564\), \(c7=0\), \(c8=0.8721876285\), \(c9=0\). Matches.

### 8. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(A*c7 + c8))`
The last term is \(c5 \exp(c6\sin(\cdot))\), which cannot be made into a plain sine term for all \(A\) by choosing constants (except trivializing it to a constant by \(c6=0\) or \(c5=0\)). If \(c5=0\), we lose the sine term entirely; if \(c6=0\), it becomes a constant \(c5 e^0=c5\), not sine. No match.

### 9. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7) + c8`
To match GT, sine term must be \(t\)-independent: set \(c5=0\). Phase 0: \(c7=0\). Remove extra terms: \(c0=0\), \(c1=0\), \(c8=0\). Then \(A*c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\sin(A c6)\) matches with \(c2=-0.3122128846\), \(c3=-0.07984001874\), \(c4=0.4717280564\), \(c6=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 10. `A**2*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(c7*t)*log(A*c8 + 1)`
As in (6), the sine is multiplied by \(e^{c3 t}\). If set \(c3=0\) to remove \(t\), then we can get a sine term, but there is no remaining \(A e^{kt}\) term (only \(A^2\), constants, and log). If keep \(c3\neq 0\), sine depends on \(t\) multiplicatively, unlike GT. No match.

### 11. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A**c2*c3*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(A*c7)*exp(c8*t) + c9`
We can set \(c6=0\) and \(c9=0\). For the sine term, need no phase: \(c5=0\), and need amplitude constant (not \(A\)-dependent), so set \(c2=0\) making \(A^{c2}=1\). Then it becomes \(A*c0 e^{c1 t} + c3\sin(A c4)\), which matches with \(c0=-0.3122128846\), \(c1=-0.07984001874\), \(c3=0.4717280564\), \(c4=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 12. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*t)*sin(A*c7 + c8) + c9`
Need sine term \(t\)-independent: set \(c6=0\), and phase \(c8=0\). Need exponential term to be \(A e^{kt}\): set \(c2=1\) so \(A^{c2}=A\). Then third term is \(A*c3 e^{c4 t}\). Remove extras: \(c0=0\), \(c1=0\), \(c9=0\). Then match with \(c3=-0.3122128846\), \(c4=-0.07984001874\), \(c5=0.4717280564\), \(c7=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 13. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(A*c3)*exp(c4*t) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`
To avoid unwanted \(e^{A c3}\) term, set \(c2=0\). Remove constant: \(c5=0\). Make sine \(t\)-independent: \(c7=0\). Remove phase: \(c9=0\). Then \(A*c0 e^{c1 t} + c6\sin(A c8)\) matches with \(c0=-0.3122128846\), \(c1=-0.07984001874\), \(c6=0.4717280564\), \(c8=0.8721876285\). Matches.

### 14. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*exp(c5*sin(A*c6 + c7))`
Both extra terms are exponentials in \(A\) / in \(\sin\), not a plain sine. They can only be removed by setting \(c2=0\) and \(c4=0\), leaving only \(A*c0 e^{c1 t}\) and no sine term. No match.

### 15. `A**4*c0*exp(A*c1) + A**2*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A**c6*c7 + c8`
Only \(t\)-dependence is in \(A*c4 e^{c5 t}\), which could match the exponential term. But there is no way to produce an additive \(\sin(0.872A)\) term from powers/exponentials in \(A\). No match.

### 16. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6 + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`
No sine term available. No match.

### 17. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2/(A*c3 + 1) + c4*Abs(A) + c5*exp(A*c6) + c7 + c8*log(A*c9 + 1)`
No sine term; cannot generate \(\sin(0.872A)\). No match.

### 18-20. (various polynomials/exponentials in \(A\) plus \(A*exp(c*t)\))
None include a sine term; cannot match GT. No match for 18, 19, 20.

### 21. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4 + c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7*log(c8*exp(A*c9) + 1)`

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.3122*A*exp(-0.0798*t) + 0.4717*sin(0.8722*A)`

This has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A*exp(decay*t)` (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
2. A `sin(c*A)` term (no t dependence)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

### Candidate 1: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5`

This has: `A*exp(c1*t)` ✓, `sin(A*c3 + c4)` which can match `sin(c3*A)` by setting c4=0 ✓, and constant c5 which can be set to 0 ✓.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`

Same as above without the constant. Set c4=0. This gives `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3)` ✓

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: `A**2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7)`

Set c0=0 (kill A²), c3=0, c5=0 (so exp(c5*t)=1), c7=0. Get: `A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c4*sin(A*c6)` ✓

**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: `A*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A**2*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`

Set c0=0, c3=0 (kill log term), c7=0, c9=0. Get: `A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c6*sin(A*c8)` ✓

**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c5=0, c7=0. Get: `A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(A*c6)` ✓

**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6 + c7*exp(c8*t)*log(c9*Abs(A) + 1)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c6=0, c7=0. Get: `c2*exp(c3*t)*sin(A*c4 + c5)`. This is `exp(t)*sin(A)` — but GT needs `A*exp(t)` term, not `exp(t)*sin(A)`. The sin term has exp(t) coupling. We need the sin term to be t-independent. Set c3=0, c5=0: `c2*sin(A*c4)`. But then we lose the `A*exp(t)` term entirely. The `A*c1` term is static. We have `c7*exp(c8*t)*log(...)` — this is log, not linear in A. Cannot produce `A*exp(t)`.

**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*exp(A*c4)*exp(c5*t) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c2=1, c4=0 → `c3*A*exp(c5*t)`, c7=0, c9=0 → `c6*sin(A*c8)` ✓

**Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(A*c7 + c8))`

The last term is `exp(sin(...))` — this is NOT a sin function. Setting c5=0 kills it, but then no sin term remains.

**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t)*sin(A*c6 + c7) + c8`

### Candidate 11: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A**c2*c3*sin(A*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(A*c7)*exp(c8*t) + c9`

Set c2=0 → c3*sin(c5) = constant, not sin(A). Set c2=1 → c3*A*sin(A*c4+c5), not sin(A). We need just sin(A), not A*sin(A). Actually if c2=0: `c3*sin(A*c4+c5)` — wait, A**0 = 1, so it's `c3*sin(A*c4+c5)` ✓. Set c6=0, c9=0, c5=0. Get: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c3*sin(A*c4)` ✓
